### Intelligent Animals

**Source**: [PCS:AA](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1601254881/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=9325&creativeASIN=1601254881&linkCode=as2&tag=httpwwwd20pfs-20)

One of the surest ways to complicate the relationship between an adventurer and her [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) is to cast [awaken](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/a/awaken) on the beast. The moment the spell takes effect, an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) ceases to be a class feature, and instead becomes a person—an NPC whose [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) has increased by 3d6 (potentially making it as smart as or smarter than the caster), and who has an increased [Charisma](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Charisma-Cha-) score and knows at least one spoken language.

An adventurer considering awakening his [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) should keep in mind the *awaken* spell’s potential drawbacks. Most pointedly, awakened [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) can no longer serve as companions, and the character must follow the rules for [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership/) if he wishes to take the animal as an official [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership). Further, an intelligent animal can be difficult to manage. After awakening, [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) are predisposed to be friendly toward whoever cast the spell— in this case, presumably their masters. Yet if an animal was mistreated during its time as a companion, or is treated poorly after its awakening, that friendliness is mixed with a sense of confusion that can last anywhere from a few moments to a few hours as the animal reconciles the abuse with the great gift it’s been given. Since *awaken* is not a [charm](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic#TOC-Enchantment-Charm) or mind-control spell, there’s nothing to prevent awakened [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) from resenting mistreatment in the same way a normal person of their intelligence level would, and they’re no more inclined to be automatically servile than anyone else. More than one careless [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) has found her awakened [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) refusing to follow instructions, leaving to pursue its own goals, or even seeking vengeance for its former “enslavement.”

On the flip side, there are many advantages to awakening an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions). If treated well, an awakened animal may become a valuable member of an adventuring party, adding new perspective to problems and fighting alongside its friends. Awakened [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) can also make stealthy and reliable snoops (for who guards her words in front of a dog?), teach adventurers about their native environments, act as guides, and provide a valuable surprise weapon against enemies who think them mere brutes. Druids, in particular, may find awakening [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) appealing—either because they wish to become true friends with their companions, or because they would value the [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal)‘ skills as allies. A devious [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid), upon witnessing an enemy mistreating its companion, may even cast *awaken* in secret upon the beast, trusting that its natural instincts will make it turn on its oppressor.

Although the personalities of awakened [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) are as varied as those of adventurers, augmented [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) often exhibit traits hearkening back to their species. Similarly, certain types of [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) may favor specific classes, battle tactics, or even weapons. The following are examples of some broad animal groups’ commonalities.

**Avians**: Raptors such as [eagles](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/eagle), [hawks](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/hawk), and [owls](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/owl)—as well as more bizarre fliers—tend to develop aloof, detached personalities, while smaller individuals are often more social and high-strung. Awakened avian [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) keenly observe the world around them—often understanding it much better than their demure natures might imply— and are adept at inferring others’ desires, motives, and intentions. These intelligent flyers are shrewdly calculating and opportunistic, especially when it comes to ensuring their own survival. Awakened birds can often be found high above a fracas, coldly deciding on the best course of action, and only entering a fray when it’s in their best interest or that of their friends.

In combat, avian [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) enjoy taking opponents by surprise, favoring training as [rogues](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) and ninjas, though they may also enjoy a [bard’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/bard) ability to soar above the fray and inspire with their songs and majestic screeches. In these capacities, the birds often use their winged stealth to their advantage, taking cover in trees and then striking quickly and silently. Awakened avian [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) use their natural weapons, but often with a twist—devious awakened flyers have been known to drop smoke shot, chain shot, and even bombs on unsuspecting enemies.

**Land Mammals (Large)**: Relishing their brute size and strength, large mammals—such as [bison](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/herd-animals/bison), [lions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/lion), and rhinoceroses—tend to divide along predator/prey lines. Herbivores tend to be generally docile but easily spooked or enraged, while predators are aggressive and cunning, constantly seeking social dominance. Whether they’re among cowering villagers or in a raiding party, these [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) love to tell stories of their physical prowess, and awakened large [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) tend to be the worst kind of braggadocios.

In combat, most large [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) gravitate toward brash, volatile tactics, becoming [barbarians](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/barbarian) or [fighters](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/fighter) who enjoy wading into battle before thinking. The exceptions are those hunters like the great [cats](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat) that rely on stealth and tracking, who are just as likely to become [rogues](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) or [rangers](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/ranger) as they are to become [barbarians](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/barbarian). Some large mammals, however, have been known to become [samurai](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/alternate-classes/samurai), replacing their natural affinity for recklessness with precision and discipline.

Large mammals recognize the value in using their [natural weapons](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Natural-Attacks), and augment those weapons in any way they can. For a [rhinoceros](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/rhinoceros), that might mean sharpening its deadly horn, while a [lion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/lion) might tip its claws with [poison](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/afflictions/poison) and a [bison](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/herd-animals/bison) might overrun its enemies with spiked chainmail affixed to its chest.

**Land Mammals (Small and Medium)**: Encompassing perhaps the widest variety of species—including creatures like [cheetahs](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/cheetah), [hyenas](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/hyena), [ponies](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/horse/pony), and [weasels](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/weasel)—Small and

Medium mammals tend to adopt mischievous, resourceful personalities when awakened. Used to living in vast ecosystems full of larger predators, these creatures are accustomed to using any advantage they have, banding together with allies or manipulating others to serve their own designs.

In battle, these [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) tend to be smart and savvy, shrewd at observing situations and determining whether it would be most advantageous to fight or run. Those [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) who prefer combat to diplomacy tend to value speed and stealth, thus making [barbarians](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/barbarian) and [rogues](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) natural choices, yet the natural curiosity of many smaller [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) may also lead them to the study of magic, from wizardry to druidism, which brings their own environments under their control. These creatures tend to be opportunistic, perpetually on the lookout for interesting magic items to help augment their natural abilities.

**Aquatic Animals**: Often as mysterious as the depths in which they live, ocean dwellers are predisposed to developing deep, philosophical personalities when awakened. The reflective natures of [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) such as [giant squid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/squid/giant-squid), [whales](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/whale), and [dolphins](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dolphin) typically manifest in one of two ways: they either find majesty in nature or adopt a religion. Once awakened, aquatic [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) also tend to be the most creative and artistic group of creatures.

Of all awakened creatures, [aquatic](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Aquatic) [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) are the most likely to become [clerics](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/cleric) or [paladins](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/paladin)—or cult leaders, for that matter. [Aquatic](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Aquatic) [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) who eschew religion may instead pursue training as [druids](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) or [bards](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/bard), or crave the intellectual stimulation of wizardry. In battle, [aquatic](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Aquatic) [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) prefer to rely on the gifts their personal beliefs provide, casting divine spells or weaving intricate battle songs and spells. As a rule, [aquatic](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Aquatic) [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) eschew combat and fight only when necessary for survival unless an enemy threatens something the animal holds sacred. Because they so dislike combat, [aquatic](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Aquatic) [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) rarely alter their [natural weapons](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Natural-Attacks).

**Primates**: Perhaps the most [human](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/core-races/human) in their perspectives, augmented primates such as [monkeys](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-monkey), [baboons](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-baboon), and [gorillas](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-gorilla) tend to have a wide range of personalities. Most are highly social and communicative, though this does not always make them great allies as they form intense attachments, manipulate others, and vie for dominance. Perhaps reflecting their impulsive personalities, primates generally pursue whatever paths seem appropriate in any given moment, and are likely to multiclass, training as anything from [barbarians](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/barbarian), [fighters](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/fighter), [rangers](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/ranger), and [rogues](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue), to exotic callings such as gunslingers and even magi. Those smaller primates used to traveling quickly through trees make great burglars and sailors, while [gorillas](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-gorilla) and [chimpanzees](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-chimpanzee) make better mercenaries and berserkers, charging into foes with terrifying force. The weapons primates wield also run the gamut. A [gorilla](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-gorilla) might choose an enormous [club](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/equipment/weapons/weapon-descriptions/club), a [chimpanzee](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-chimpanzee) a two-handed sword that lets him take advantage of his tremendous strength, and a [monkey](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-monkey) a hand crossbow or [blunderbuss](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/equipment/weapons/weapon-descriptions/blunderbuss).

**Reptiles**: From the [lizard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/lizard/lizard-common) to the [constrictor snake](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/snake/snake-constrictor) to the [ankylosaurus](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dinosaur/ankylosaurus), awakened reptiles tend to be haughty and disdainful toward others. They eschew company whenever possible, preferring instead to be alone with their increasingly complex thoughts. Although their gruff exteriors can be off-putting, once an adventurer has earned an awakened reptile’s friendship, it lasts for a lifetime.

When they are forced to pursue a discipline, smaller reptiles favor esoteric orders and studies, perhaps becoming [druids](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid), [oracles](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/oracle), or even [witches](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/witch), while larger reptiles—such as [dinosaurs](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dinosaur)—are often content to remain savagely effective [barbarians](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/barbarian). Poisonous creatures might become [rogues](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue), ninjas, and assassins, supplementing their own poisons with those of others. Though not necessarily evil, reptiles often retain predatory streaks that can seem cruel to others, and some crave violence and the thrill of the hunt over all. In combat, as in most things, reptiles rarely show anger or passion, instead pursuing their goals with cold, emotionless drive, their expressions nearly impossible for other creatures to read.

### Controlling Companions

How a companion works depends on the campaign as well as the companion’s nature, intelligence, and abilities. In some cases, the rules do not specify whether you or the GM controls the companion. If you’re entirely in control, the companion acts like a subsidiary PC, doing exactly what you want just like a true PC. If the GM is control, you can make suggestions or attempt to influence the companion, but the GM determines whether the creature is willing or able to attempt what you want.

#### Aspects of Control

Whether you or the GM controls a particular companion depends largely on the creature’s intelligence and level of independence from you.

**Nonsentient Companions**: a nonsentient companion (one with animal-level intelligence) is loyal to you in the way a well-trained [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) is—the creature is conditioned to obey your commands, but its behavior is limited by its intelligence and it can’t make altruistic moral decisions—such as nobly sacrificing itself to save another. [Animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), [cavalier](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/cavalier) mounts, and purchased creatures (such as common horses and guard [dogs](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog)) fall into this category. In general they’re GM-controlled companions. You can direct them using the [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal) skill, but their specific behavior is up to the GM.

**Sentient Companions**: a sentient companion (a creature that can understand language and has an [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) score of at least 3) is considered your ally and obeys your suggestions and orders to the best of its ability. It won’t necessarily blindly follow a suicidal order, but it has your interests at heart and does what it can to keep you alive. [Paladin](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/paladin) bonded mounts, familiars, and cohorts fall into this category, and are usually player-controlled companions.

**Eidolons**: Outside the linear obedience and intelligence scale of sentient and nonsentient companions are eidolons: intelligent entities magically bound to you. Whether you wish to roleplay this relationship as friendly or coerced, the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) is inclined to obey you unless you give a [command](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/c/command) only to spite it. An [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) would obey a cruel [summoner’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner) order to save a child from a burning building, knowing that at worst the fire damage would temporarily banish it, but it wouldn’t stand in a bonfire just because the [summoner](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner) said to. An [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) is normally a player-controlled companion, but the GM can have the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) refuse extreme orders that would cause it to suffer needlessly.

**Magical Control**: [Charm person](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/c/charm-person), [dominate person](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/d/dominate-person), and similar effects turn an NPC into a companion for a limited time. Most [charm](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic#TOC-Enchantment-Charm)-like effects make the target friendly to you—the target has to follow your requests only if they’re reasonable, and has its own ideas about what is reasonable. For example, few creatures consider “hand over all your valuables” or “let me put these manacles on you” a reasonable request from a friend. You might have to use [Diplomacy](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/diplomacy) or [Intimidate](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/intimidate) checks to influence a charmed ally, and the GM has the final say as to what happens. Though the target of a [charm](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic#TOC-Enchantment-Charm) effect considers you a friend, it probably feels indifferent at best toward the other PCs and won’t listen to requests from them. a creature under a dominate effect is more of a puppet, and you can force it to do anything that isn’t suicidal or otherwise against its well-being. Treat it as player-controlled, with the GM making its saving throws to resist inappropriate commands.

**Common Exceptions**: Some companions are exceptions, such as an intelligent companion who doesn’t bear exceptional loyalty toward you (for example, a hired guard), a weaker minion who is loyal to you but lacks the abilities or resources to assist in adventuring tasks, and a called [outsider](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Outsider) (such as from [planar ally](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/p/planar-ally)) who agrees to a specific service but still has a sense of self-preservation. You can use [Bluff](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/bluff), [Diplomacy](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/diplomacy), and [Intimidate](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/intimidate) to influence such companions, but the GM is the final arbiter of their actions. For example, a PC might use threats to convince a caravan guard to hold back an [ogre](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/humanoids/giants/ogre) for a few rounds or to prevent her zealous followers from attacking a rival adventurer, but the GM makes the decision whether the guard runs away after getting hit once or the followers attack when provoked.

The GM may deviate from the above suggestions, such as allowing a [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) to control an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) directly, creating a more equivalent or even antagonistic relationship between a [summoner](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner) and an [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon), or roleplaying a mentoring relationship between a veteran warhorse and the young [paladin](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/paladin) who inherited his loyalty. Before you create a character with a companion creature (or decide to add a companion in play), the GM should explain to everyone how much influence you and the GM each have over the creature’s actions. That way, everyone is fully informed about all aspects of dealing with the companion.

The specifics of controlling a companion vary for different campaigns. a gritty campaign where [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) can’t do anything that real [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) can’t do forces the GM to act as a check against you pushing the bounds of creativity. a high-fantasy game where familiars are nearly as important to the storyline as the PCs—or are played as near-PCs by other players—is a very different feel and can create interesting roleplaying opportunities.

An evil campaign where companions are unwilling slaves of the PCs creates a dynamic where the PCs are trying to exploit them as much as possible—perhaps even sacrificing and replacing them as needed—and treat them more like living tools than reluctant allies.

#### Issues of Control

The GM should keep in mind several factors when it comes to companions, whether handling them as suggested above or altering the balance to give you more or less control.

**Ease of Play**: Changing who controls a companion can make the game easier or harder for the GM. Controlling a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) in combat is one more complex thing for the GM to deal with. The GM must keep track of a [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) tactics and motivations and how those affect it in combat while keeping her own knowledge of the monsters separate from the [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) knowledge; otherwise, the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) will outshine the PCs with superior tactics. Giving you control over these decisions (while still allowing the GM to veto certain actions) alleviates some of the burden and allows you to plan interesting tactics between yourself and your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), much as you would have mastered during times you trained together.

Conversely, giving a player full control over the actions of two characters can slow down the game. If you’re prone to choice paralysis, playing two turns every round can drag the game to a halt. If this is a problem, the GM should suggest that another player help run the companion or ask you to give up the companion and alter yourself to compensate (such as by choosing a different feat in place of [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership/), taking a domain instead of a [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), or selecting the “companions” option for a [ranger’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/ranger) hunter’s bond ability instead of an animal).

**Game Balance**: Even a simple change like allowing players to directly control companions has repercussions in the game mechanics. For example, if a [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) has complete control over an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), there’s no reason for her to put ranks in [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal), freeing up those ranks for other valuable skills like [Perception](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/perception). If a [wizard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) with a guard [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) doesn’t have to use a [move action](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Move-Actions) to make a [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal) check to have the [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) attack, he has a full set of actions each round and a minion creature that doesn’t require investing any extra time to “[summon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Summon-Sp-)” it. If companion [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) don’t have to know specific tricks, the PC can use any animal like an ally and plan strategies (like [flanking](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Flanking)) as if the animal were much smarter than it actually is.

With intelligent companions such as cohorts, giving you full control means you’re controlling two characters and can take twice as many actions as the other players. The GM can create a middle ground, such as requiring you to put ranks in [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal) but not requiring you to make checks, or reducing the action needed to command an animal, but these decisions should be made before the companion joins the group.

**Sharing Information**: Whenever you control multiple creatures, there are issues of sharing information between you and your companions. Some companions have special abilities that facilitate this sort of communication, such as a [familiar’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard#TOC-Arcane-Bond-Ex-or-Sp-) empathic link or an [eidolon’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) bond senses ability, but most companions are limited to what they can observe with their own senses. For example, if a [wizard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) using [see invisibility](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/s/see-invisibility) knows there is an [invisible](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/conditions#TOC-Invisible) [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) across the room, he can’t just direct his guard [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) to attack the [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue); he has to use the seek command to move the [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) to the general area of the [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue), and even then he can’t use the attack command to attack the [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) because the [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) isn’t an “apparent enemy.” If the GM allows the [wizard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) to make the [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) fight the [invisible](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/conditions#TOC-Invisible) [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue), that makes the animal much more versatile than normal, and also devalues the special nature of a true empathic or [telepathic bond](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/t/telepathic-bond) with a companion. If the [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) is allowed to work outside the PC’s line of sight, it devalues abilities such as a [wizard’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) ability to scry on his [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar). Of course, intelligent companions using speech can bypass some of these limitations (such as telling a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) there’s an [invisible](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/conditions#TOC-Invisible) [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) in the corner).

#### Advancing Companions

Another issue is who gets to control the companion’s advancement. [Animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), eidolons, and cohorts all advance much like PCs, making choices about feats, skills, special abilities, and (in the case of cohorts) class levels. Whoever controls the companion’s actions also makes decisions about its advancement, but there is more of a shared role between you and the GM for some types of companions.

**Animal Companion**: Advancement choices for an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) include feats, skills, ability score increases, and tricks.

If the companion’s [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) score is 2 or lower, it is limited to a small selection of feats. You should decide what feats the animal learns, though the GM should have a say about whether a desired feat is appropriate to the animal’s type and training—fortunately, the feats on the list are appropriate for just about any animal. If the animal’s [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) is 3 or higher (whether from using its ability score increase or a magic item), it can select any feat that it qualifies for. You should decide what feat it learns, subject to GM approval, although the creature’s higher intelligence might mean it has its own ideas about what it wants to learn.

As with feats, you should decide what skills your [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) learns, chosen from the [Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) Skills list and subject to GM approval. If the animal’s [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) score is 3 or higher, it can put its ranks into any skill, with the GM’s approval. Of course, the animal might not have the physical ability to perform certain skills (a [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) can’t create disguises, an [elephant](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/elephant/elephant) can’t use the [Ride](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/ride) skill, and so on).

Ability score increases are straightforward when it comes to physical ability scores—training an animal to be stronger, more agile, or tougher are all reasonable tasks. Training an animal to be smarter, more intuitive, or more self-aware is less easy to justify—except in the context where people can cast spells and [speak with animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/s/speak-with-animals).

Because you’re responsible for using the [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal) skill to teach your companion its tricks, you decide what tricks the companion learns. If you’re not skilled at training [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) or lack the time to do it yourself, you can hire an expert trainer to do it for you or use the downtime system to take care of this training.

**Cohort**: Advancement choices for a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) include feats, skills, ability score increases, and class levels.

A [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) is generally considered a player-controlled companion, and therefore you get to decide how the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) advances. The GM might step in if you make choices that are inappropriate for the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), use the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) as a mechanism for pushing the boundaries of the game rules, or treat the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) unfairly. a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) is a loyal companion and ally to you, and expects you to treat him fairly, generously, without aloofness or cruelty, and without devoting too much attention to other minions such as familiars or [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions). The [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) attitude toward you is generally helpful (as if using the [Diplomacy](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/diplomacy) skill); he complies with most of your requests without any sort of skill check, except for requests that are against his nature or put him in serious peril.

If you exploit your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), you’ll quickly find your [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership/) score shrinking away. Although this doesn’t change the [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) level, the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) can’t gain levels until your [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership/) score allows for a level increase, so if you’re a poor leader, you must wait longer for your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) to level up. In extreme cases, the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) might abandon you, and you’ll have to recruit a new [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership).

Examples of inappropriate advancement choices are a good-aligned companion selecting morally questionable feats, a clumsy [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) suddenly putting many ranks in [Disable Device](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/disable-device) (so he can take all the risks in searching for traps instead of you), a spellcaster [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) taking nothing but [item creation](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/item-creation-feats) feats (so you get access to plenty of cheap magic items at the cost of just one feat, [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership)), a [fighter](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/fighter) [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) taking a level in [wizard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) when he had no previous interest in magic, or you not interacting with your [cleric](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/cleric) [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) other than to gain defensive spells from a different class or a [flanking](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Flanking) bonus.

When you select the [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) feat, you and the GM should discuss the [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) background, personality, interests, and role in the campaign and party. Not only does this give the GM the opportunity to reject a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) concept that goes against the theme of the campaign, but the GM can plan adventure hooks involving the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) for future quests. The [random background generator](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/more-character-options/pfbggen) can help greatly when filling in details about the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership). Once the discussion is done, writing down a biography and personality profile of the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) helps cement his role in the campaign and provides a strong reference point for later talks about what is or is not appropriate advancement for the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership).

**Eidolon**: Compared to an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) or [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), an [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) is a unique type of companion—it is intelligent and loyal to you, and you have absolute power over whether it is present in the material world or banished to its home plane. You literally have the power to reshape the [eidolon’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) body using the [transmogrify](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/t/transmogrify) spell, and though technically the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) can resist this—the Saving Throw is “[Will](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Will) negates (harmless)”—it is assumed that the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) complies with what you want. After all, the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) can’t actually be killed while summoned; at worst, it might experience pain before damage sends it back to its home plane. This means the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) is usually willing to take great risks to help you. If swimming through acid was the only way to save you, it would do so, knowing that it won’t die and will recover. The [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) is a subservient creature whose very nature depends upon your will, so you decide what feats, skill points, ability score increases, and evolutions the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) gains as it advances.

**Follower**: Because a follower is much lower level than you, it’s generally not worth determining a follower’s exact feats and skill ranks, as he would be ineffective against opponents appropriate for your level. In most cases, knowing the follower’s name, gender, race, class, level, and profession is sufficient, such as “Lars, male [human](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/core-races/human) expert 1, sailor.” Since followers lack full stat blocks, the issue of advancing them is irrelevant. If your [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) score improves, just add new followers rather than advancing existing ones. However, if events require advancing a follower (such as turning a follower into a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) to replace a [dead](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/conditions#TOC-Dead) [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership)), use the same guidelines as for cohorts.

**Hirelings**: Hirelings don’t normally gain levels. If the GM is running a kingdom-building campaign where hireling NPCs are heavily involved, you might suggest ways for NPCs to advance, but the final decision is up to the GM. If you want more control over your hireling’s feats, skills, and class levels, you should select that hireling as a follower with the [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) feat.

**Mounts**: Common mounts (such as horses or [riding dogs](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/riding-dog) bought from a merchant, rather than mounts that are class features) don’t normally advance. If extraordinary circumstances merit a mount gaining [Hit Dice](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/glossary#TOC-Hit-Dice-HD-), and you have [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal) ranks and take an interest in training the animal, use the same guidelines as those for [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions).

### Intelligent Animals

Increasing an animal’s [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) to 3 or higher means it is smart enough to understand a language. However, unless an [awaken](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/a/awaken) spell is used, the animal doesn’t automatically and instantly learn a language, any more than a [human](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/core-races/human) child does. The animal must be taught a language, usually over the course of months, giving it the understanding of the meaning of words and sentences beyond its trained responses to commands like “attack” and “heel.”

Even if the animal is taught to understand a language, it probably lacks the anatomy to actually speak (unless [awaken](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/a/awaken) is used). For example, [dogs](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog), [elephants](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/elephant/elephant), and even [gorillas](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-gorilla) lack the proper physiology to speak [humanoid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Humanoid) languages, though they can use their limited “vocabulary” of sounds to articulate concepts, especially if working with a person who learns what the sounds mean.

An intelligent animal is smart enough to use tools, but might lack the ability to manipulate them. a crow could be able to use simple lockpicks, but a [dog](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dog/dog) can’t. Even if the animal is physically capable of using a tool, it might still prefer its own natural body to manufactured items, especially when it comes to weapons. An intelligent [gorilla](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/primates/primate-gorilla) could hold or wield a sword, but its inclination is to make slam attacks. No amount of training (including weapon proficiency feats) is going to make it fully comfortable attacking in any other way.

Even if an animal’s [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) increases to 3 or higher, you must still use the [Handle Animal](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/skills/handle-animal) skill to direct the animal, as it is a smart animal rather than a low-intelligence person (using [awaken](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/a/awaken) is an exception—an awakened animal takes orders like a person). The GM should take the animal’s [Intelligence](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Intelligence-Int-) into account when determining its response to commands or its behavior when it doesn’t have specific instructions. For example, an intelligent [wolf](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/undead/ghoul-wolf-1) companion can pick the weakest-looking target if directed to do so, and that same [wolf](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/undead/ghoul-wolf-1) trapped in a burning building might push open a door or window without being told.

### Remembering Companions and Followers

There are several ways to make sure a companion doesn’t get lost or forgotten.

**Props**: Physical props can help you, the other players, and the GM remember companions. If the campaign uses miniatures on the tabletop, the companion should have its own miniature or token. If all the adventurers move forward, it’s easy to see that a lonely miniature was left behind. Even without miniatures, having a physical representation of the companion on the tabletop keeps it in mind. Whether this is a stuffed animal, a toy, an action figure, a cardboard stand-up, a GameMastery Face Card, or a simple character sheet with a colorful illustration, this kind of reminder gives the companion a presence on the tabletop.

**Another Player**: If you regularly forget the presence of your companion and the GM is busy dealing with the rest of the game, another player can take over playing the companion. If the second player has an introverted character or one whose actions in combat are fast and efficient, allowing that player to control the companion gives him another opportunity to have some time in the spotlight. The second player should roll [initiative](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Initiative) separately for the companion so the companion’s actions don’t get forgotten on either turn—giving the companion its own turn reinforces its role in the party.

Allowing another character to play the companion also gives the group additional roleplaying opportunities. You might feel silly talking as both your character and your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), but more comfortable having a dialogue with your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) when it’s played by someone else (this also keeps the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) from blindly doing whatever you say). Wearing a hat or mask, or holding up a small flag or banner to represent the companion can help other players keep track of who is acting when you speak.

**Casual Observer**: Some gaming groups have a casual player, friend, spouse, or child who isn’t interested in playing a normal character for the campaign, but likes to watch the game or be nearby when everyone else is playing. That person might be interested in playing a companion for one or more sessions (especially if it’s a creature that’s funny and cute). This is an opportunity for that person to get involved in the game without the responsibility of being a full contributing member to the group—and just might be the hook that convinces that observer to become active in the game.

If playing a companion goes well, the GM may create a one-shot spin-off adventure in which all the players play companion creatures instead of normal PCs (perhaps because the PCs are captured, incapacitated, or merely sleeping), returning to the normal campaign when that adventure is completed.

Often, a companion is forgotten about when it’s not needed. a [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard#TOC-Arcane-Bond-Ex-or-Sp-) hides in a backpack and only comes out when the [sorcerer](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/sorcerer) needs to spy on something or deliver a spell with a range of [touch](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Touch-Attacks). An [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) or [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) follows the [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) silently and acts only when a skill check or [attack roll](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Attack-Roll) is needed. An [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) is used as a mount or an expendable resource in battle. You and the GM need to remember that a companion is a creature, not an unthinking tool, and can’t simply be ignored.

Followers are a little more complex because there can be so many of them and they don’t usually adventure with you. You and the GM should keep notes about each follower (or group of followers, if there are several in a common location such as a temple) and link this information to the followers’ base of operations. For example, the GM’s notes about the capital city should mention the thieves’ guild informant follower of the [rogue](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/rogue) PC. Artwork representing the follower (even a simple piece of free clip art found online) can be a stronger reminder than a name that’s easily lost in a page full of words.

Followers also have a unique companion role in that they spend most of their time away from you, and might use that time positively or negatively. Just because a follower is low level and you’re not doesn’t mean the follower stops being a person with needs, fears, and a role to play in your heroic story. Even if you dismiss the follower aspect of the [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) feat as baggage, a follower is going to pay attention to what you do, and if this hero-worship grows tarnished from neglect or abuse, that very same follower provides an opportunity for the GM to demonstrate how bad will among the common folk can negatively affect an adventurer’s life (see [Reputation](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/other-rules/reputation-and-fame) for more information).

### Companion Plot Hooks

Having a companion in the party is an incredible opportunity for the GM to introduce plot elements into a campaign—and more interesting plots than “the companion has been kidnapped!” The players have a general idea about their characters’ pre-adventurer histories, but a companion is a bit of a mystery. What did it do before it met you? What is its motivation for joining the adventuring party? What are its goals? What does it do when you aren’t around?

#### Animal Companion

Unless you raised your [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) from birth, it has its own history and secrets that are likely important and could [surprise](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Surprise) you. a [druid’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) [wolf](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/undead/ghoul-wolf-1) companion might have been saved by a famous [ranger](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/ranger), fought in an [orc](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/other-races/featured-races/arg-orc) tribe’s arena, or escaped a [wizard’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) experimental lab. What happens when that [wolf](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/undead/ghoul-wolf-1) recognizes that helpful [ranger](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/ranger), savage [orc](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/other-races/featured-races/arg-orc), or mad [wizard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard)? Is the [wolf](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/undead/ghoul-wolf-1) aggressive when the [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) isn’t around? Does it have behavior quirks like not letting anyone [touch](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Touch-Attacks) the [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) when she’s sleeping, even allies trying to wake her? What if the companion was once a [humanoid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Humanoid), but was cursed or polymorphed into a different shape and lost its memory about its original identity? What if another [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) previously cast [awaken](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/a/awaken) on it, and it has been pretending to be a common animal so it can watch over or spy on a PC? The answers to these questions are the seeds to side plots or entire adventures.

[Animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) can also incite [fear](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/special-abilities#TOC-Fear) or prejudice among ignorant townsfolk. Most villages don’t want rowdy adventurers bringing [wolves](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/canines/wolf/), [bears](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/bear), [lions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/lion), [giant](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Giant) [snakes](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/snake), and especially [dinosaurs](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/dinosaur) into the town square, and innkeepers don’t usually want the larger [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) staying in rooms with guests. Stables might charge more to board exotic [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) or entirely refuse to do so, and might not have appropriate food for them. If a village is experiencing attacks on its livestock, angry people might be quick to blame a carnivorous [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions). Conversely, innocent children could have a circus-like fascination with exotic [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) and help break the ice between visiting adventurers and suspicious locals.

#### Cohort

A [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) could have a former life as a criminal that she abandoned after being inspired by your heroic deeds. Just like a PC, a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) has family and friends, with hopes and concerns for those people. The [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) might be a target for your enemies who are unwilling or unable to strike directly at you (though be careful to avoid making the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) become a liability or look incompetent). a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) who is critically injured by a monster might develop a fear about that kind of monster and avoid attacking it. She may have secret vices or virtues that become more prominent over time and can directly affect her relationship with you. If the [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) has an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), you might also suffer some indirect repercussions for the animal’s behavior or reputation.

#### Eidolon

An [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) has the same mystery as a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), except its origins are far weirder. It might have been linked to another [summoner](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner) before its bond with you. It might be a [natural](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/glossary#TOC-Natural-Armor-Bonus) creature altered by planar energies and banished to a far realm, or a former adventurer lost in a disastrous mission to an unknown plane. If it resembles a more conventional planar monster (such as an [archon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Archon), a [dretch](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/outsiders/demon/dretch), or an [elemental](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Elemental)), it might have been accidentally summoned or called by a sloppy spellcaster and could have some familiarity with other people in the world. Though an [eidolon’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) soul is strongly tied to its [summoner](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner), it has an existence in another world when it is away, and in that world it might be a bully, champion, or slave. How it reacts to things during its limited time on the [Material Plane](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/environment/the-planes#TOC-Material-Plane1) is influenced by its unknown past and secret life.

An [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) always has the appearance of a fantastical creature, and attracts as much attention as any unfamiliar animal would. Fortunately for you, you can send the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) away to its [extraplanar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Extraplanar) home, allowing you to do business in town and move about normally without drawing unwanted attention. However, if you call the [eidolon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/base-classes/summoner#TOC-Eidolon) in an emergency without warning the local authorities, townsfolk might assume it is a marauding monster bent on tearing them limb from limb, requiring hasty explanations and diplomacy to prevent panic.

#### Familiar

Plot hooks for familiars are similar to those for [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), as they can have the same unknown backgrounds and instinctive reactions to people they knew when they were just common [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal). Fortunately, familiars are usually small creatures that can easily pass for common pets as long as they don’t do anything that reveals their unusual intelligence. Most townsfolk aren’t averse to a common [cat](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat), a trained [hawk](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/hawk), or even a [snake](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/snake), though innkeepers and merchants might ask that such [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) be kept in a cage to prevent them from getting loose and causing any damage.

Remember that a [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard#TOC-Arcane-Bond-Ex-or-Sp-) has an empathic link to its master, and its animal instincts can lead to plot hooks. For example, a [toad](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/toad) [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar) might project feelings of hunger whenever a member of a fly-[demon](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Demon) cult is nearby, a [bat](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/bat/bat) [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar) might express curiosity about the words a weird hermit is muttering under his breath, and a [rat](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/rat/rat-common) [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar) might feel fear when a dangerous assassin walks into the room. A more powerful [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar) can speak with other [animals](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/creature-types#TOC-Animal) of its kind, and if left to roam, it could pick up interesting news about a town or an army camp.

#### Follower

A follower should be more than an acquaintance or an employee. a follower is devoted to you in the same way a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) is, but has fewer resources at his disposal and in most cases isn’t an adventurer. The follower sees you as a hero or celebrity—someone to emulate. Though it’s easy to treat followers as a single, nameless group, a smart player realizes that they don’t have to group together. Followers can be spread out over multiple settlements and have multiple roles. For example, if you have a [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) score of 10, you can have five 1st-level followers: a city guard in the capital, an acolyte at the high temple, an informant in the thieves’ guild, an adept in a frontier village, and a strange child saved from a [goblin’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/other-races/featured-races/arg-goblin) hunger. Gaining followers is an opportunity for you to look back over your adventuring career, recall important or noteworthy NPCs, and solidify the bonds between those NPCs and you.

Choosing followers gives you a network of loyal contacts who trust and respect you. Though they might not have the resources or backbone to fight on your behalf, they’re always on the lookout for ways to help you in any way they can. In effect, they are trustworthy NPC contacts (Trust score 4; see [Contacts](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/more-character-options/ultimate-campaign-contacts)). The city guard might invite you to gamble with the other guards or arrange to have your armor polished. The acolyte might have tips about an upcoming religious festival and the clergy’s concerns about a nearby plague. The informant might have news about mysterious disappearances or volunteer to keep an eye on your rival. a thug might bully the truth out of a tight-lipped witness or provide inside information on her employer. The adept might send messages about strange events from the wildlands. The strange child might have precognitive visions, perhaps from budding magical powers.

If you ever lose or dismiss your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), selecting a replacement from among your followers not only gives you an excuse to spend some downtime training that follower to become your new [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), but rewards the loyalty of all the other followers, as they see that you treat them as near equals.

The GM should use these followers as plot hooks. Instead of having rumors from an unknown source reach your ears from no specific source, a named follower could present that information. Instead of having you hunt for information about a cataclysm prophesied to occur in 3 days, a scholarly follower could find a scroll or book about the prophecy and bring it to you. The desperate stable-boy follower can approach you about money to pay off his father’s gambling debts to a crooked bookkeeper. The poor merchant can ask you for help dealing with a charismatic man trying to convince his daughter to become a prostitute. By using a follower for a plot hook, the GM lets the player know that the character can trust the follower’s intentions, and keeps the PC’s past involvement with that NPC relevant.

As you reach higher [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) scores, you gain dozens of followers. Rather than these followers all being spread thinly across every possible settlement in the campaign, it’s more likely that many of these individual followers know each other well, possibly by working together, spending time at the same temple or academy, or being members of the same family, and you should expand these clusters of followers in an organic way. For example, the other guards who gamble with you could become new followers, the acolyte can train other acolytes or spread the good word about you, the informant might persuade others in the thieves’ guild that you’re a valuable ally, the adept’s entire village might begin to see you as a hero and savior, and the strange child could become a [wizard’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard) apprentice and convince the entire cabal to befriend you. If you ever decide to build a fort or found a temple or guild, you already have a group of like-minded and skilled followers ready and willing to help.

### Reviving And Replacing Companions

Adventuring is a dangerous career, and sometimes an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), or [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar) dies or is lost. a change in your [alignment](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/glossary#TOC-Alignment) or religion might drive away your [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), or the [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) role in the story might end based on discussion between you and the GM. An [extended](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/metamagic-feats/extend-spell-metamagic) voyage in a dangerous environment might convince a [druid](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid) to free a trusted companion that would otherwise suffer and die if forced to travel (such as a [polar bear](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/bear/polar-bear) in the desert). a [ranger](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/ranger) might discover a rare specimen of a favorite type of creature and want to claim it as his own in order to protect it from poachers. Regardless of the cause, when a companion dies or is lost, you need to replace it. This creates an opportunity for roleplaying.

#### Reviving a Dead Companion

A lost [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar), or follower can be raised or resurrected with spells such as [raise dead](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/r/raise-dead), [resurrection](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/r/resurrection), or [true resurrection](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/t/true-resurrection). For a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) or follower with character levels, these kinds of spells give the character one or more [negative levels](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/special-abilities#TOC-Energy-Drain-and-Negative-Levels)—a price worth paying if the alternative is death. Creatures with no character levels (such as [animal companions](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) and familiars) count as 1st level for the purpose of these spells, and therefore they take [Constitution drain](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Ability-Drain) instead of [negative levels](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/special-abilities#TOC-Energy-Drain-and-Negative-Levels). a nonsentient companion is assumed to be willing to return to life unless you were cruel to it or directly responsible for its death.

In most cases, the companion probably remembers its last moments alive and understands that you’re the reason why it is alive again. For a lower-level [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) or a non-adventuring follower, the gift of a second chance at life is something very treasured and earns you great respect and devotion. You can gain the reputation of “fairness and generosity” for the purposes of the [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) feat.

Using [reincarnate](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/magic/all-spells/r/reincarnate) is an alternative option, but has a similar effect on a companion’s loyalty and affection. Few [humans](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/core-races/human) would choose to be reincarnated as a [bugbear](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/humanoids/bugbear) or [kobold](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/races/other-races/featured-races/arg-kobold), but if the choice is that or death, a new life in a new body is generally preferred. For an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions), the GM should create a random table of creatures similar to its original form—for example, a [lion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/lion) might be reincarnated as a [leopard](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/leopard), [cheetah](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/cheetah), or [tiger](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/cat-great/tiger).

#### Finding a Replacement

In some cases, replacing an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) or [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/animals/familiar) can be as easy as purchasing an animal of the desired type and declaring it your new companion. Attuning a [familiar](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/wizard#TOC-Arcane-Bond-Ex-or-Sp-) to its new master requires a ritual. Choosing an [animal companion](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/classes/core-classes/druid/animal-companions/animal-companions) requires 24 hours of prayer. The ceremony can also be used to attract and bond with an animal appropriate to the local environment. However, you might want to wait for the campaign to present an appropriate companion, such as an animal you rescue from a cruel enemy that you tame with the ritual or ceremony. In terms of game mechanics, there is no difference between any of these options, and you should work with the GM to find a replacement method that is appropriate to the campaign.

Replacing a lost or killed [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) or follower involves a similar collaboration between you and the GM to create a character who is appropriate for the campaign and valuable to you (and hopefully to the rest of the party). You might want to elevate a follower to a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), select another known NPC to become a [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership), or start from scratch by introducing a new NPC to the party. Keep in mind that your [Leadership](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) score might have changed, especially if you were responsible for the previous [cohort’s](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership) death—and that sort of tragedy creates roleplaying opportunities for the new [cohort](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/leadership).

#### Ankheg

**Source**: Speak with Animals: Magical Beast Companions 1

This companion is available via the [Beast Speaker feat](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/beast-speaker/). The 11th-level mastery benefit is given if the character takes the [Beast Speaker Mastery feat](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/feats/general-feats/beast-speaker-mastery/).

Starting Statistics

**Size** Medium; **Speed** 30 ft., [burrow](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Burrow-Ex-) 20 ft.; **AC** +5 [natural armor](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/glossary#TOC-Natural-Armor-Bonus); **Attack** bite (1d8 plus 1d4 acid and [grab](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Grab-Ex-)); **Ability Scores** **Str** 12, **Dex** 12, **Con** 15, **Int** 1, **Wis** 13, **Cha** 6; **Special Qualities** [darkvision](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/special-abilities#TOC-Darkvision) 60 ft., [low-light vision](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/special-abilities#TOC-Low-Light-Vision), [tremorsense](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Tremorsense-Ex-) 60 ft.; **CMD** +8 vs. [trip](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Trip)

9th-Level Advancement

**Size** Large; **AC** +2 [natural armor](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/glossary#TOC-Natural-Armor-Bonus); **Attack** bite (2d6 plus 1d4 acid and [grab](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/rules-for-monsters/universal-monster-rules#TOC-Grab-Ex-)); **Ability Scores** **Str** +4, **Dex** -2, **Con** +2; **Special Attacks** spit acid

#### Spit Acid (Ex)

Once every 6 hours, the [ankheg](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/magical-beasts/ankheg) can spit a 30-foot line of acid. Creatures struck by this acid take 4d4 points of acid damage. A [Reflex](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/gamemastering/combat#TOC-Reflex) save halves the damage (save is [Con](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/basics-ability-scores/ability-scores#TOC-Constitution-Con-) based). Once used, the [ankheg](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/magical-beasts/ankheg) must wait 6 hours to be able to use it again. During the waiting period, the [ankheg](https://www.d20pfsrd.com/bestiary/monster-listings/magical-beasts/ankheg)‘s bite loses its acid damage.

#### Ant, Riding

**Source**: [JBE:CM](http://www.opengamingstore.com/collections/jon-brazer-enterprises/products/cavalier-mounts)

**Special** A cavalier can choose this as a mount.

Starting Statistics
